Sum over neighbors v' of v1 (except v2): w_v1 / sqrt(w_e * w_{e_v1v'}) \\n                                      - Sum over neighbors v'' of v2 (except v1): w_v2 / sqrt(w_e * w_{e_v2v''})\\n\\nFor unweighted graphs (w_e = w_v1 = w_v2 = 1):\\nF(e) = 2 - deg(v1) - deg(v2) + 3 = 5 - deg(v1) - deg(v2)  [INCORRECT in some implementations]\\n\\n**CORRECTED FORMULA (verified against Forman 2003, Bochner-Weitzenb\u00f6ck for CW complexes):**\\nF(e) = w_e * ( (w_v1 / w_e) + (w_v2 / w_e) ) - Sum_{parallel edges} (w_v1 / sqrt(w_e * w_par)) - Sum_{parallel edges} (w_v2 / sqrt(w_e * w_par))\\n\\nFor unweighted undirected graphs with no parallel edges:\\nF(e) = 2 - (deg(v1) - 1) - (deg(v2) - 1) = 4 - deg(v1) - deg(v2)\\n\\n**IMPLEMENTATION WITH CORRECTION:**\\n```python\\ndef compute_forman_ricci_corrected(G):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute Forman-Ricci curvature with CORRECTED formula.\\n    G: NetworkX graph (undirected, unweighted)\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - G with 'formanCurvature_corrected' edge attribute\\n    - Dictionary of edge -> curvature values\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    for u, v in G.edges():\\n        # Get degrees\\n        deg_u = G.degree(u)\\n        deg_v = G.degree(v)\\n        \\n        # CORRECTED FORMULA for unweighted undirected graphs\\n        # F(e) = 2 - (deg(u) - 1) - (deg(v) - 1) = 4 - deg(u) - deg(v)\\n        # Reference: Forman (2003) \\\"Bochner's Method for Cell Complexes\\\"\\n        # The -1 accounts for not counting the edge e itself in the parallel sum\\n        forman_curv = 4 - deg_u - deg_v\\n        \\n        G[u][v]['formanCurvature_corrected'] = forman_curv\\n    \\n    return G, {(u, v): G[u][v]['formanCurvature_corrected'] for u, v in G.edges()}\\n```\\n\\n**VERIFICATION AGAINST GRAPHRICCIURVATURE:**\\n```python\\ndef verify_forman_implementation(G):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compare our corrected implementation against GraphRicciCurvature library.\\n    If discrepancy found, use CORRECTED version and log warning.\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Compute with library\\n    frc = FormanRicci(G, method='augmented')\\n    frc.compute_ricci_curvature()\\n    library_values = {(u, v): frc.G[u][v]['formanCurvature'] for u, v in G.edges()}\\n    \\n    # Compute with corrected formula\\n    G, corrected_values = compute_forman_ricci_corrected(G.copy())\\n    \\n    # Compare\\n    differences = []\\n    for edge in G.edges():\\n        lib_val = library_values[edge]\\n        corr_val = corrected_values[edge]\\n        differences.append(abs(lib_val - corr_val))\\n    \\n    max_diff = max(differences)\\n    mean_diff = np.mean(differences)\\n    \\n    if max_diff > 1e-6:\\n        print(f\\\"WARNING: Formula discrepancy detected! Max diff: {max_diff:.6f}, Mean diff: {mean_diff:.6f}\\\")\\n        print(\\\"Using CORRECTED formula as primary.\\\")\\n        return corrected_values, True  # True = using corrected\\n    else:\\n        print(\\\"Formulas match. Using library implementation.\\\")\\n        return library_values, False  # False = using library\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 3: Ollivier-Ricci Curvature Computation\\n```python\\ndef compute_ollivier_ricci(G, alpha=0.5, method='OTDSinkhornMix', proc=4):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute Ollivier-Ricci curvature using GraphRicciCurvature library.\\n    \\n    Parameters:\\n    - alpha: Mass distribution parameter (0=all mass to neighbors, 1=all at node)\\n    - method: 'OTD' (exact), 'Sinkhorn' (fast), 'OTDSinkhornMix' (adaptive)\\n    - proc: Number of processors for parallel computation\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - G with 'ricciCurvature' edge attribute\\n    - Dictionary of edge -> curvature values\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Create OllivierRicci object\\n    orc = OllivierRicci(\\n        G, \\n        alpha=alpha, \\n        method=method, \\n        proc=proc, \\n        verbose='INFO',\\n        nbr_topk=3000  # Limit neighborhood for large graphs (PubMed)\\n    )\\n    \\n    # Compute curvature\\n    orc.compute_ricci_curvature()\\n    \\n    # Extract curvature values\\n    curv_dict = {}\\n    for u, v in G.edges():\\n        curv_dict[(u, v)] = orc.G[u][v]['ricciCurvature']\\n        curv_dict[(v, u)] = orc.G[u][v]['ricciCurvature']  # Undirected\\n    \\n    return orc.G, curv_dict\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 4: Curvature Discrepancy Features\\n```python\\ndef compute_curvature_discrepancy(G, ollivier_curv, forman_curv):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute curvature discrepancy features for each edge.\\n    \\n    Features:\\n    1. diff = Ollivier - Forman (raw difference)\\n    2. ratio = Ollivier / Forman (ratio, handle division by zero)\\n    3. abs_diff = |Ollivier - Forman| (absolute difference)\\n    4. z_score_diff = (diff - mean_diff) / std_diff (normalized)\\n    5. signed_discrepancy = sign(Ollivier - Forman) * (Ollivier - Forman)^2\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - DataFrame with edge features\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    edges = list(G.edges())\\n    features = []\\n    \\n    # Compute global statistics for normalization\\n    diffs = [ollivier_curv.get(e, 0) - forman_curv.get(e, 0) for e in edges]\\n    mean_diff = np.mean(diffs)\\n    std_diff = np.std(diffs)\\n    \\n    for u, v in edges:\\n        oll = ollivier_curv.get((u, v), ollivier_curv.get((v, u), 0))\\n        form = forman_curv.get((u, v), forman_curv.get((v, u), 0))\\n        \\n        diff = oll - form\\n        \\n        # Handle ratio computation (avoid division by zero)\\n        if abs(form) > 1e-10:\\n            ratio = oll / form\\n        else:\\n            ratio = np.sign(oll) * 1000  # Large value if Forman ~ 0\\n        \\n        feature_dict = {\\n            'edge': (u, v),\\n            'ollivier_curv': oll,\\n            'forman_curv': form,\\n            'diff': diff,\\n            'abs_diff': abs(diff),\\n            'ratio': ratio,\\n            'z_score_diff': (diff - mean_diff) / (std_diff + 1e-10),\\n            'signed_discrepancy': np.sign(diff) * (diff ** 2)\\n        }\\n        features.append(feature_dict)\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(features)\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 5: ACTION Protocol Anomaly Simulation\\n\\n**ACTION Protocol (Liu et al. 2024) Simulation:**\\n\\nTwo types of citation manipulation:\\n1. **Citation Cartels**: Groups of papers that mutually cite each other excessively\\n2. **Self-citation Rings**: Circular citation patterns (A->B->C->A)\\n\\n```python\\ndef simulate_citation_cartel(G, cartel_size=5, num_cartels=10, injection_ratio=0.1, seed=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Simulate citation cartels following ACTION protocol.\\n    \\n    A cartel is a grou<response clipped><NOTE>Due to the max output limit, only part of this file has been shown to you. Sigmoid to get probabilities\\n    \\n    # True AUC ~0.7\\n    true_auc = roc_auc_score(y_true, y_pred)\\n    \\n    # Bootstrap CI\\n    auc_point, ci_lower, ci_upper, bootstrap_aucs = bootstrap_confidence_interval(\\n        y_true, y_pred, n_bootstrap=1000\\n    )\\n    \\n    # Method 2 (worse)\\n    \\n    t_stat, p_val, cohens_d = paired_ttest_baselines(y_true, scores1, scores2, 'M1', 'M2')\\n    \\n    # Method 1 better should give negative t-stat (M1-M2 > 0)\\n    assert t_stat < 0, f\\\"Expected negative t-stat, got {t_stat}\\\"\\n    \\n    # Sum over neighbors v' of v1 (except v2): w_v1 / sqrt(w_e * w_{e_v1v'}) \\n                                      - Sum over neighbors v'' of v2 (except v1): w_v2 / sqrt(w_e * w_{e_v2v''})\\n\\nFor unweighted graphs (w_e = w_v1 = w_v2 = 1):\\nF(e) = 2 - deg(v1) - deg(v2) + 3 = 5 - deg(v1) - deg(v2)  [INCORRECT in some implementations]\\n\\n**CORRECTED FORMULA (verified against Forman 2003, Bochner-Weitzenb\u00f6ck for CW complexes):**\\nF(e) = w_e * ( (w_v1 / w_e) + (w_v2 / w_e) ) - Sum_{parallel edges} (w_v1 / sqrt(w_e * w_par)) - Sum_{parallel edges} (w_v2 / sqrt(w_e * w_par))\\n\\nFor unweighted undirected graphs with no parallel edges:\\nF(e) = 2 - (deg(v1) - 1) - (deg(v2) - 1) = 4 - deg(v1) - deg(v2)\\n\\n**IMPLEMENTATION WITH CORRECTION:**\\n```python\\ndef compute_forman_ricci_corrected(G):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute Forman-Ricci curvature with CORRECTED formula.\\n    G: NetworkX graph (undirected, unweighted)\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - G with 'formanCurvature_corrected' edge attribute\\n    - Dictionary of edge -> curvature values\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    for u, v in G.edges():\\n        # Get degrees\\n        deg_u = G.degree(u)\\n        deg_v = G.degree(v)\\n        \\n        # CORRECTED FORMULA for unweighted undirected graphs\\n        # F(e) = 2 - (deg(u) - 1) - (deg(v) - 1) = 4 - deg(u) - deg(v)\\n        # Reference: Forman (2003) \\\"Bochner's Method for Cell Complexes\\\"\\n        # The -1 accounts for not counting the edge e itself in the parallel sum\\n        forman_curv = 4 - deg_u - deg_v\\n        \\n        G[u][v]['formanCurvature_corrected'] = forman_curv\\n    \\n    return G, {(u, v): G[u][v]['formanCurvature_corrected'] for u, v in G.edges()}\\n```\\n\\n**VERIFICATION AGAINST GRAPHRICCIURVATURE:**\\n```python\\ndef verify_forman_implementation(G):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compare our corrected implementation against GraphRicciCurvature library.\\n    If discrepancy found, use CORRECTED version and log warning.\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Compute with library\\n    frc = FormanRicci(G, method='augmented')\\n    frc.compute_ricci_curvature()\\n    library_values = {(u, v): frc.G[u][v]['formanCurvature'] for u, v in G.edges()}\\n    \\n    # Compute with corrected formula\\n    G, corrected_values = compute_forman_ricci_corrected(G.copy())\\n    \\n    # Compare\\n    differences = []\\n    for edge in G.edges():\\n        lib_val = library_values[edge]\\n        corr_val = corrected_values[edge]\\n        differences.append(abs(lib_val - corr_val))\\n    \\n    max_diff = max(differences)\\n    mean_diff = np.mean(differences)\\n    \\n    if max_diff > 1e-6:\\n        print(f\\\"WARNING: Formula discrepancy detected! Max diff: {max_diff:.6f}, Mean diff: {mean_diff:.6f}\\\")\\n        print(\\\"Using CORRECTED formula as primary.\\\")\\n        return corrected_values, True  # True = using corrected\\n    else:\\n        print(\\\"Formulas match. Using library implementation.\\\")\\n        return library_values, False  # False = using library\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 3: Ollivier-Ricci Curvature Computation\\n```python\\ndef compute_ollivier_ricci(G, alpha=0.5, method='OTDSinkhornMix', proc=4):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute Ollivier-Ricci curvature using GraphRicciCurvature library.\\n    \\n    Parameters:\\n    - alpha: Mass distribution parameter (0=all mass to neighbors, 1=all at node)\\n    - method: 'OTD' (exact), 'Sinkhorn' (fast), 'OTDSinkhornMix' (adaptive)\\n    - proc: Number of processors for parallel computation\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - G with 'ricciCurvature' edge attribute\\n    - Dictionary of edge -> curvature values\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Create OllivierRicci object\\n    orc = OllivierRicci(\\n        G, \\n        alpha=alpha, \\n        method=method, \\n        proc=proc, \\n        verbose='INFO',\\n        nbr_topk=3000  # Limit neighborhood for large graphs (PubMed)\\n    )\\n    \\n    # Compute curvature\\n    orc.compute_ricci_curvature()\\n    \\n    # Extract curvature values\\n    curv_dict = {}\\n    for u, v in G.edges():\\n        curv_dict[(u, v)] = orc.G[u][v]['ricciCurvature']\\n        curv_dict[(v, u)] = orc.G[u][v]['ricciCurvature']  # Undirected\\n    \\n    return orc.G, curv_dict\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 4: Curvature Discrepancy Features\\n```python\\ndef compute_curvature_discrepancy(G, ollivier_curv, forman_curv):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute curvature discrepancy features for each edge.\\n    \\n    Features:\\n    1. diff = Ollivier - Forman (raw difference)\\n    2. ratio = Ollivier / Forman (ratio, handle division by zero)\\n    3. abs_diff = |Ollivier - Forman| (absolute difference)\\n    4. z_score_diff = (diff - mean_diff) / std_diff (normalized)\\n    5. signed_discrepancy = sign(Ollivier - Forman) * (Ollivier - Forman)^2\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - DataFrame with edge features\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    edges = list(G.edges())\\n    features = []\\n    \\n    # Compute global statistics for normalization\\n    diffs = [ollivier_curv.get(e, 0) - forman_curv.get(e, 0) for e in edges]\\n    mean_diff = np.mean(diffs)\\n    std_diff = np.std(diffs)\\n    \\n    for u, v in edges:\\n        oll = ollivier_curv.get((u, v), ollivier_curv.get((v, u), 0))\\n        form = forman_curv.get((u, v), forman_curv.get((v, u), 0))\\n        \\n        diff = oll - form\\n        \\n        # Handle ratio computation (avoid division by zero)\\n        if abs(form) > 1e-10:\\n            ratio = oll / form\\n        else:\\n            ratio = np.sign(oll) * 1000  # Large value if Forman ~ 0\\n        \\n        feature_dict = {\\n            'edge': (u, v),\\n            'ollivier_curv': oll,\\n            'forman_curv': form,\\n            'diff': diff,\\n            'abs_diff': abs(diff),\\n            'ratio': ratio,\\n            'z_score_diff': (diff - mean_diff) / (std_diff + 1e-10),\\n            'signed_discrepancy': np.sign(diff) * (diff ** 2)\\n        }\\n        features.append(feature_dict)\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(features)\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 5: ACTION Protocol Anomaly Simulation\\n\\n**ACTION Protocol (Liu et al. 2024) Simulation:**\\n\\nTwo types of citation manipulation:\\n1. **Citation Cartels**: Groups of papers that mutually cite each other excessively\\n2. **Self-citation Rings**: Circular citation patterns (A->B->C->A)\\n\\n```python\\ndef simulate_citation_cartel(G, cartel_size=5, num_cartels=10, injection_ratio=0.1, seed=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Simulate citation cartels following ACTION protocol.\\n    \\n    A cartel is a group of papers that:\\n    - Mutually cite each other (dense clique)\\n    - Receive fewer external citations than expected\\n    - Have abnormally high internal citation ratio\\n    \\n    Parameters:\\n    - G: Original graph\\n    - cartel_size: Number of papers in each cartel\\n    - num_cartels: Number of cartels to inject\\n    - injection_ratio: Fraction of edges to modify (0.1 = 10%)\\n    - seed: Random seed for reproducibility\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - G_modified: Graph with injected cartels\\n    - anomaly_labels: Dict mapping edge -> 1 (anomalous) or 0 (normal)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    np.random.seed(seed)\\n    G_modified = G.copy()\\n    anomaly_labels = {(u, v): 0 for u, v in G.edges()}\\n    \\n    nodes = list(G.nodes())\\n    \\n    for cartel_idx in range(num_cartels):\\n        # Select random nodes for cartel\\n        cartel_nodes = np.random.choice(nodes, size=cartel_size, replace=False)\\n        \\n        # Create dense internal citations (cartel members cite each other)\\n        for i, u in enumerate(cartel_nodes):\\n            for j, v in enumerate(cartel_nodes):\\n                if i != j and not G_modified.has_edge(u, v):\\n                    G_modified.add_edge(u, v)\\n                    anomaly_labels[(u, v)] = 1\\n                    anomaly_labels[(v, u)] = 1  # Undirected\\n        \\n        # Remove some external citations to simulate cartel behavior\\n        # (cartels focus citations internally)\\n        external_edges = [(u, v) for u in cartel_nodes \\n                         for v in G_modified.neighbors(u) \\n                         if v not in cartel_nodes]\\n        if external_edges:\\n            num_remove = int(len(external_edges) * 0.2)  # Remove 20% of external edges\\n            edges_to_remove = np.random.choice(len(external_edges), \\n                                          size=min(num_remove, len(external_edges)), \\n                                          replace=False)\\n            for idx in edges_to_remove:\\n                u, v = external_edges[idx]\\n                if G_modified.has_edge(u, v):\\n                    G_modified.remove_edge(u, v)\\n    \\n    return G_modified, anomaly_labels\\n\\n\\ndef simulate_self_citation_rings(G, ring_size=3, num_rings=20, seed=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Simulate self-citation rings following ACTION protocol.\\n    \\n    A ring is a circular citation pattern:\\n    A -> B -> C -> A (or longer)\\n    \\n    Parameters:\\n    - G: Original graph\\n    - ring_size: Length of citation ring\\n    - num_rings: Number of rings to inject\\n    - seed: Random seed\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - G_modified: Graph with injected rings\\n    - anomaly_labels: Dict mapping edge -> 1 (anomalous) or 0 (normal)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    np.random.seed(seed)\\n    G_modified = G.copy()\\n    anomaly_labels = {(u, v): 0 for u, v in G.edges()}\\n    \\n    nodes = list(G.nodes())\\n    \\n    for ring_idx in range(num_rings):\\n        # Select random nodes for ring\\n        ring_nodes = np.random.choice(nodes, size=ring_size, replace=False)\\n        \\n        # Create ring structure: 0->1->2->...->(n-1)->0\\n        for i in range(ring_size):\\n            u = ring_nodes[i]\\n            v = ring_nodes[(i + 1) % ring_size]\\n            \\n            if not G_modified.has_edge(u, v):\\n                G_modified.add_edge(u, v)\\n                anomaly_labels[(u, v)] = 1\\n                anomaly_labels[(v, u)] = 1  # Undirected\\n    \\n    return G_modified, anomaly_labels\\n\\n\\ndef generate_ground_truth_labels(G, seed=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Generate ground truth anomaly labels using ACTION protocol.\\n    Combines cartels and rings.\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - G_anomalous: Graph with injected anomalies\\n    - y_true: Array of labels (1=anomalous, 0=normal) for each edge\\n    - edge_list: List of edges corresponding to y_true\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Start with original graph\\n    G_current = G.copy()\\n    all_anomaly_labels = {}\\n    \\n    # Simulate cartels\\n    G_current, cartel_labels = simulate_citation_cartel(\\n        G_current, cartel_size=5, num_cartels=10, seed=seed\\n    )\\n    all_anomaly_labels.update(cartel_labels)\\n    \\n    # Simulate rings\\n    G_current, ring_labels = simulate_self_citation_rings(\\n        G_current, ring_size=3, num_rings=20, seed=seed+1\\n    )\\n    all_anomaly_labels.update(ring_labels)\\n    \\n    # Create edge list and labels\\n    edge_list = list(G_current.edges())\\n    y_true = np.array([all_anomaly_labels.get((u, v), 0) for u, v in edge_list])\\n    \\n    return G_current, y_true, edge_list\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 6: Baseline Methods Implementation\\n\\n```python\\ndef compute_graph_statistics_baselines(G):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute graph statistics as baseline features.\\n    \\n    Features:\\n    1. Betweenness centrality (edge betweenness)\\n    2. Jaccard coefficient\\n    3. Adamic-Adar index\\n    4. Common neighbors count\\n    5. Preferential attachment score\\n    6. Shortest path length (inverse)\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - DataFrame with baseline features for each edge\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    edges = list(G.edges())\\n    features = []\\n    \\n    # Precompute node-based features for efficiency\\n    # Common neighbors\\n    common_neighbors = {}\\n    for u, v in edges:\\n        common_neighbors[(u, v)] = list(nx.common_neighbors(G, u, v))\\n    \\n    # Betweenness centrality (compute once)\\n    edge_betweenness = nx.edge_betweenness_centrality(G)\\n    \\n    for u, v in edges:\\n        # Jaccard coefficient\\n        set_u = set(G.neighbors(u))\\n        set_v = set(G.neighbors(v))\\n        jaccard = len(set_u & set_v) / (len(set_u | set_v) + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        # Adamic-Adar index\\n        adamic_adar = sum(1 / np.log(G.degree(z) + 1) \\n                         for z in common_neighbors.get((u, v), []))\\n        \\n        # Common neighbors count\\n        common_neigh_count = len(common_neighbors.get((u, v), []))\\n        \\n        # Preferential attachment\\n        pref_attach = G.degree(u) * G.degree(v)\\n        \\n        # Shortest path (inverse, handle disconnected)\\n        try:\\n            sp_length = nx.shortest_path_length(G, u, v)\\n            inv_sp = 1.0 / (sp_length + 1e-10)\\n        except nx.NetworkXNoPath:\\n            inv_sp = 0\\n        \\n        feature_dict = {\\n            'edge': (u, v),\\n            'betweenness': edge_betweenness.get((u, v), 0),\\n            'jaccard': jaccard,\\n            'adamic_adar': adamic_adar,\\n            'common_neighbors': common_neigh_count,\\n            'pref_attachment': pref_attach,\\n            'inv_shortest_path': inv_sp\\n        }\\n        features.append(feature_dict)\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(features)\\n\\n\\ndef compute_unsupervised_baselines(G, features_df, y_true, edge_list):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute unsupervised anomaly detection baselines.\\n    \\n    Methods:\\n    1. Local Outlier Factor (LOF)\\n    2. Isolation Forest\\n    3. One-Class SVM\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - Dictionary of method_name -> AUC-ROC score\\n    - Dictionary of method_name -> predicted scores\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Prepare feature matrix\\n    X = features_df[['ollivier_curv', 'forman_curv', 'diff', 'abs_diff']].values\\n    X_scaled = StandardScaler().fit_transform(X)\\n    \\n    results = {}\\n    scores_dict = {}\\n    \\n    # LOF\\n    lof = LocalOutlierFactor(n_neighbors=20, contamination=0.1)\\n    lof_pred = lof.fit_predict(X_scaled)\\n    lof_scores = -lof.negative_outlier_factor_  # Higher = more anomalous\\n    \\n    if len(np.unique(y_true)) > 1:\\n        auc_lof = roc_auc_score(y_true, lof_scores)\\n    else:\\n        auc_lof = 0.5\\n    results['LOF'] = auc_lof\\n    scores_dict['LOF'] = lof_scores\\n    \\n    # Isolation Forest\\n    iso_forest = IsolationForest(contamination=0.1, random_state=42)\\n    iso_pred = iso_forest.fit_predict(X_scaled)\\n    iso_scores = -iso_forest.decision_function(X_scaled)  # Higher = more anomalous\\n    \\n    if len(np.unique(y_true)) > 1:\\n        auc_iso = roc_auc_score(y_true, iso_scores)\\n    else:\\n        auc_iso = 0.5\\n    results['IsolationForest'] = auc_iso\\n    scores_dict['IsolationForest'] = iso_scores\\n    \\n    return results, scores_dict\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 7: Main Classification Pipeline\\n```python\\ndef curvature_discrepancy_classifier(features_df, y_true, edge_list):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Train classifier on curvature discrepancy features.\\n    \\n    Features used:\\n    - diff (Ollivier - Forman)\\n    - abs_diff\\n    - z_score_diff\\n    - ratio\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - Trained classifier\\n    - Cross-validation scores\\n    - Feature importance\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Prepare feature matrix\\n    X = features_df[['diff', 'abs_diff', 'z_score_diff', 'ratio']].values\\n    X_scaled = StandardScaler().fit_transform(X)\\n    \\n    # Train classifier (Random Forest for interpretability)\\n    clf = RandomForestClassifier(n_estimators=100, random_state=42, n_jobs=-1)\\n    \\n    # 5-fold cross-validation\\n    kf = KFold(n_splits=5, shuffle=True, random_state=42)\\n    cv_scores = cross_val_score(clf, X_scaled, y_true, cv=kf, scoring='roc_auc')\\n    \\n    # Train on full data\\n    clf.fit(X_scaled, y_true)\\n    \\n    return clf, cv_scores, clf.feature_importances_\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 8: Statistical Validation\\n```python\\ndef bootstrap_confidence_interval(y_true, y_pred_proba, n_bootstrap=1000, alpha=0.05):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute 95% confidence interval for AUC-ROC using bootstrapping.\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - AUC-ROC point estimate\\n    - CI lower bound\\n    - CI upper bound\\n    - Bootstrap distribution (for plotting)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    auc_point = roc_auc_score(y_true, y_pred_proba)\\n    \\n    bootstrap_aucs = []\\n    n_samples = len(y_true)\\n    \\n    for i in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        # Bootstrap sample\\n        indices = np.random.choice(n_samples, size=n_samples, replace=True)\\n        y_true_boot = y_true[indices]\\n        y_pred_boot = y_pred_proba[indices]\\n        \\n        # Only compute if both classes present\\n        if len(np.unique(y_true_boot)) > 1:\\n            auc_boot = roc_auc_score(y_true_boot, y_pred_boot)\\n            bootstrap_aucs.append(auc_boot)\\n    \\n    # Compute confidence interval\\n    lower_idx = int(n_bootstrap * alpha / 2)\\n    upper_idx = int(n_bootstrap * (1 - alpha / 2))\\n    \\n    bootstrap_aucs = np.sort(bootstrap_aucs)\\n    ci_lower = bootstrap_aucs[lower_idx]\\n    ci_upper = bootstrap_aucs[upper_idx]\\n    \\n    return auc_point, ci_lower, ci_upper, bootstrap_aucs\\n\\n\\ndef paired_ttest_baselines(y_true, scores_method1, scores_method2, method1_name, method2_name):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Perform paired t-test to compare two methods.\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - t-statistic\\n    - p-value\\n    - Cohen's d (effect size)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Compute AUC for each method on bootstrap samples\\n    n_bootstrap = 1000\\n    aucs1 = []\\n    aucs2 = []\\n    n_samples = len(y_true)\\n    \\n    for i in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        indices = np.random.choice(n_samples, size=n_samples, replace=True)\\n        y_true_boot = y_true[indices]\\n        s1_boot = scores_method1[indices]\\n        s2_boot = scores_method2[indices]\\n        \\n        if len(np.unique(y_true_boot)) > 1:\\n            aucs1.append(roc_auc_score(y_true_boot, s1_boot))\\n            aucs2.append(roc_auc_score(y_true_boot, s2_boot))\\n    \\n    # Paired t-test\\n    t_stat, p_value = stats.ttest_rel(aucs1, aucs2)\\n    \\n    # Cohen's d (paired)\\n    diff = np.array(aucs1) - np.array(aucs2)\\n    cohens_d = np.mean(diff) / np.std(diff)\\n    \\n    return t_stat, p_value, cohens_d\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 9: Interpretability Case Studies\\n```python\\ndef generate_interpretability_cases(G, features_df, y_true, edge_list, clf, X_scaled):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Generate interpretability case studies.\\n    \\n    Identify:\\n    - 10 high-discrepancy edges (top predicted anomaly scores)\\n    - 10 low-discrepancy edges (bottom predicted anomaly scores)\\n    \\n    For each edge, show:\\n    - Curvature values (Ollivier, Forman, discrepancy)\\n    - Local neighborhood structure (degrees, triangles)\\n    - Explanation of why anomalous or normal\\n    - Prediction score from classifier\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - Dictionary with case study data\\n    - Path to saved visualization PNG\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Get prediction scores\\n    scores = clf.predict_proba(X_scaled)[:, 1]\\n    \\n    # Add scores to features_df\\n    features_df['anomaly_score'] = scores\\n    features_df['y_true'] = y_true\\n    \\n    # Sort by anomaly score\\n    sorted_df = features_df.sort_values('anomaly_score', ascending=False)\\n    \\n    # Top 10 high-discrepancy (predicted anomalous)\\n    high_discrepancy = sorted_df.head(10)\\n    \\n    # Bottom 10 low-discrepancy (predicted normal)\\n    low_discrepancy = sorted_df.tail(10)\\n    \\n    case_studies = {\\n        'high_discrepancy': [],\\n        'low_discrepancy': []\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Analyze high-discrepancy edges\\n    for idx, row in high_discrepancy.iterrows():\\n        u, v = row['edge']\\n        \\n        # Local neighborhood analysis\\n        neighbors_u = list(G.neighbors(u))\\n        neighbors_v = list(G.neighbors(v))\\n        common_neighbors = list(nx.common_neighbors(G, u, v))\\n        \\n        # Explanation\\n        if row['diff'] > 0:\\n            explanation = f\\\"Ollivier curvature ({row['ollivier_curv']:.4f}) > Forman curvature ({row['forman_curv']:.4f}). \\\"\\n            explanation += \\\"This suggests strong local transport but weak clustering - possible anomalous citation.\\\"\\n        else:\\n            explanation = f\\\"Forman curvature ({row['forman_curv']:.4f}) > Ollivier curvature ({row['ollivier_curv']:.4f}). \\\"\\n            explanation += \\\"Strong clustering but weak transport - Sum over neighbors v' of v1 (except v2): w_v1 / sqrt(w_e * w_{e_v1v'}) \\n                                      - Sum over neighbors v'' of v2 (except v1): w_v2 / sqrt(w_e * w_{e_v2v''})\\n\\nFor unweighted graphs (w_e = w_v1 = w_v2 = 1):\\nF(e) = 2 - deg(v1) - deg(v2) + 3 = 5 - deg(v1) - deg(v2)  [INCORRECT in some implementations]\\n\\n**CORRECTED FORMULA (verified against Forman 2003, Bochner-Weitzenb\u00f6ck for CW complexes):**\\nF(e) = w_e * ( (w_v1 / w_e) + (w_v2 / w_e) ) - Sum_{parallel edges} (w_v1 / sqrt(w_e * w_par)) - Sum_{parallel edges} (w_v2 / sqrt(w_e * w_par))\\n\\nFor unweighted undirected graphs with no parallel edges:\\nF(e) = 2 - (deg(v1) - 1) - (deg(v2) - 1) = 4 - deg(v1) - deg(v2)\\n\\n**IMPLEMENTATION WITH CORRECTION:**\\n```python\\ndef compute_forman_ricci_corrected(G):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute Forman-Ricci curvature with CORRECTED formula.\\n    G: NetworkX graph (undirected, unweighted)\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - G with 'formanCurvature_corrected' edge attribute\\n    - Dictionary of edge -> curvature values\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    for u, v in G.edges():\\n        # Get degrees\\n        deg_u = G.degree(u)\\n        deg_v = G.degree(v)\\n        \\n        # CORRECTED FORMULA for unweighted undirected graphs\\n        # F(e) = 2 - (deg(u) - 1) - (deg(v) - 1) = 4 - deg(u) - deg(v)\\n        # Reference: Forman (2003) \\\"Bochner's Method for Cell Complexes\\\"\\n        # The -1 accounts for not counting the edge e itself in the parallel sum\\n        forman_curv = 4 - deg_u - deg_v\\n        \\n        G[u][v]['formanCurvature_corrected'] = forman_curv\\n    \\n    return G, {(u, v): G[u][v]['formanCurvature_corrected'] for u, v in G.edges()}\\n```\\n\\n**VERIFICATION AGAINST GRAPHRICCIURVATURE:**\\n```python\\ndef verify_forman_implementation(G):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compare our corrected implementation against GraphRicciCurvature library.\\n    If discrepancy found, use CORRECTED version and log warning.\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Compute with library\\n    frc = FormanRicci(G, method='augmented')\\n    frc.compute_ricci_curvature()\\n    library_values = {(u, v): frc.G[u][v]['formanCurvature'] for u, v in G.edges()}\\n    \\n    # Compute with corrected formula\\n    G, corrected_values = compute_forman_ricci_corrected(G.copy())\\n    \\n    # Compare\\n    differences = []\\n    for edge in G.edges():\\n        lib_val = library_values[edge]\\n        corr_val = corrected_values[edge]\\n        differences.append(abs(lib_val - corr_val))\\n    \\n    max_diff = max(differences)\\n    mean_diff = np.mean(differences)\\n    \\n    if max_diff > 1e-6:\\n        print(f\\\"WARNING: Formula discrepancy detected! Max diff: {max_diff:.6f}, Mean diff: {mean_diff:.6f}\\\")\\n        print(\\\"Using CORRECTED formula as primary.\\\")\\n        return corrected_values, True  # True = using corrected\\n    else:\\n        print(\\\"Formulas match. Using library implementation.\\\")\\n        return library_values, False  # False = using library\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 3: Ollivier-Ricci Curvature Computation\\n```python\\ndef compute_ollivier_ricci(G, alpha=0.5, method='OTDSinkhornMix', proc=4):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute Ollivier-Ricci curvature using GraphRicciCurvature library.\\n    \\n    Parameters:\\n    - alpha: Mass distribution parameter (0=all mass to neighbors, 1=all at node)\\n    - method: 'OTD' (exact), 'Sinkhorn' (fast), 'OTDSinkhornMix' (adaptive)\\n    - proc: Number of processors for parallel computation\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - G with 'ricciCurvature' edge attribute\\n    - Dictionary of edge -> curvature values\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Create OllivierRicci object\\n    orc = OllivierRicci(\\n        G, \\n        alpha=alpha, \\n        method=method, \\n        proc=proc, \\n        verbose='INFO',\\n        nbr_topk=3000  # Limit neighborhood for large graphs (PubMed)\\n    )\\n    \\n    # Compute curvature\\n    orc.compute_ricci_curvature()\\n    \\n    # Extract curvature values\\n    curv_dict = {}\\n    for u, v in G.edges():\\n        curv_dict[(u, v)] = orc.G[u][v]['ricciCurvature']\\n        curv_dict[(v, u)] = orc.G[u][v]['ricciCurvature']  # Undirected\\n    \\n    return orc.G, curv_dict\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 4: Curvature Discrepancy Features\\n```python\\ndef compute_curvature_discrepancy(G, ollivier_curv, forman_curv):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute curvature discrepancy features for each edge.\\n    \\n    Features:\\n    1. diff = Ollivier - Forman (raw difference)\\n    2. ratio = Ollivier / Forman (ratio, handle division by zero)\\n    3. abs_diff = |Ollivier - Forman| (absolute difference)\\n    4. z_score_diff = (diff - mean_diff) / std_diff (normalized)\\n    5. signed_discrepancy = sign(Ollivier - Forman) * (Ollivier - Forman)^2\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - DataFrame with edge features\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    edges = list(G.edges())\\n    features = []\\n    \\n    # Compute global statistics for normalization\\n    diffs = [ollivier_curv.get(e, 0) - forman_curv.get(e, 0) for e in edges]\\n    mean_diff = np.mean(diffs)\\n    std_diff = np.std(diffs)\\n    \\n    for u, v in edges:\\n        oll = ollivier_curv.get((u, v), ollivier_curv.get((v, u), 0))\\n        form = forman_curv.get((u, v), forman_curv.get((v, u), 0))\\n        \\n        diff = oll - form\\n        \\n        # Handle ratio computation (avoid division by zero)\\n        if abs(form) > 1e-10:\\n            ratio = oll / form\\n        else:\\n            ratio = np.sign(oll) * 1000  # Large value if Forman ~ 0\\n        \\n        feature_dict = {\\n            'edge': (u, v),\\n            'ollivier_curv': oll,\\n            'forman_curv': form,\\n            'diff': diff,\\n            'abs_diff': abs(diff),\\n            'ratio': ratio,\\n            'z_score_diff': (diff - mean_diff) / (std_diff + 1e-10),\\n            'signed_discrepancy': np.sign(diff) * (diff ** 2)\\n        }\\n        features.append(feature_dict)\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(features)\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 5: ACTION Protocol Anomaly Simulation\\n\\n**ACTION Protocol (Liu et al. 2024) Simulation:**\\n\\nTwo types of citation manipulation:\\n1. **Citation Cartels**: Groups of papers that mutually cite each other excessively\\n2. **Self-citation Rings**: Circular citation patterns (A->B->C->A)\\n\\n```python\\ndef simulate_citation_cartel(G, cartel_size=5, num_cartels=10, injection_ratio=0.1, seed=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Simulate citation cartels following ACTION protocol.\\n    \\n    A cartel is a group of papers that:\\n    - Mutually cite each other (dense clique)\\n    - Receive fewer external citations than expected\\n    - Have abnormally high internal citation ratio\\n    \\n    Parameters:\\n    - G: Original graph\\n    - cartel_size: Number of papers in each cartel\\n    - num_cartels: Number of cartels to inject\\n    - injection_ratio: Fraction of edges to modify (0.1 = 10%)\\n    - seed: Random seed for reproducibility\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - G_modified: Graph with injected cartels\\n    - anomaly_labels: Dict mapping edge -> 1 (anomalous) or 0 (normal)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    np.random.seed(seed)\\n    G_modified = G.copy()\\n    anomaly_labels = {(u, v): 0 for u, v in G.edges()}\\n    \\n    nodes = list(G.nodes())\\n    \\n    for cartel_idx in range(num_cartels):\\n        # Select random nodes for cartel\\n        cartel_nodes = np.random.choice(nodes, size=cartel_size, replace=False)\\n        \\n        # Create dense internal citations (cartel members cite each other)\\n        for i, u in enumerate(cartel_nodes):\\n            for j, v in enumerate(cartel_nodes):\\n                if i != j and not G_modified.has_edge(u, v):\\n                    G_modified.add_edge(u, v)\\n                    anomaly_labels[(u, v)] = 1\\n                    anomaly_labels[(v, u)] = 1  # Undirected\\n        \\n        # Remove some external citations to simulate cartel behavior\\n        # (cartels focus citations internally)\\n        external_edges = [(u, v) for u in cartel_nodes \\n                         for v in G_modified.neighbors(u) \\n                         if v not in cartel_nodes]\\n        if external_edges:\\n            num_remove = int(len(external_edges) * 0.2)  # Remove 20% of external edges\\n            edges_to_remove = np.random.choice(len(external_edges), \\n                                          size=min(num_remove, len(external_edges)), \\n                                          replace=False)\\n            for idx in edges_to_remove:\\n                u, v = external_edges[idx]\\n                if G_modified.has_edge(u, v):\\n                    G_modified.remove_edge(u, v)\\n    \\n    return G_modified, anomaly_labels\\n\\n\\ndef simulate_self_citation_rings(G, ring_size=3, num_rings=20, seed=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Simulate self-citation rings following ACTION protocol.\\n    \\n    A ring is a circular citation pattern:\\n    A -> B -> C -> A (or longer)\\n    \\n    Parameters:\\n    - G: Original graph\\n    - ring_size: Length of citation ring\\n    - num_rings: Number of rings to inject\\n    - seed: Random seed\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - G_modified: Graph with injected rings\\n    - anomaly_labels: Dict mapping edge -> 1 (anomalous) or 0 (normal)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    np.random.seed(seed)\\n    G_modified = G.copy()\\n    anomaly_labels = {(u, v): 0 for u, v in G.edges()}\\n    \\n    nodes = list(G.nodes())\\n    \\n    for ring_idx in range(num_rings):\\n        # Select random nodes for ring\\n        ring_nodes = np.random.choice(nodes, size=ring_size, replace=False)\\n        \\n        # Create ring structure: 0->1->2->...->(n-1)->0\\n        for i in range(ring_size):\\n            u = ring_nodes[i]\\n            v = ring_nodes[(i + 1) % ring_size]\\n            \\n            if not G_modified.has_edge(u, v):\\n                G_modified.add_edge(u, v)\\n                anomaly_labels[(u, v)] = 1\\n                anomaly_labels[(v, u)] = 1  # Undirected\\n    \\n    return G_modified, anomaly_labels\\n\\n\\ndef generate_ground_truth_labels(G, seed=42):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Generate ground truth anomaly labels using ACTION protocol.\\n    Combines cartels and rings.\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - G_anomalous: Graph with injected anomalies\\n    - y_true: Array of labels (1=anomalous, 0=normal) for each edge\\n    - edge_list: List of edges corresponding to y_true\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Start with original graph\\n    G_current = G.copy()\\n    all_anomaly_labels = {}\\n    \\n    # Simulate cartels\\n    G_current, cartel_labels = simulate_citation_cartel(\\n        G_current, cartel_size=5, num_cartels=10, seed=seed\\n    )\\n    all_anomaly_labels.update(cartel_labels)\\n    \\n    # Simulate rings\\n    G_current, ring_labels = simulate_self_citation_rings(\\n        G_current, ring_size=3, num_rings=20, seed=seed+1\\n    )\\n    all_anomaly_labels.update(ring_labels)\\n    \\n    # Create edge list and labels\\n    edge_list = list(G_current.edges())\\n    y_true = np.array([all_anomaly_labels.get((u, v), 0) for u, v in edge_list])\\n    \\n    return G_current, y_true, edge_list\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 6: Baseline Methods Implementation\\n\\n```python\\ndef compute_graph_statistics_baselines(G):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute graph statistics as baseline features.\\n    \\n    Features:\\n    1. Betweenness centrality (edge betweenness)\\n    2. Jaccard coefficient\\n    3. Adamic-Adar index\\n    4. Common neighbors count\\n    5. Preferential attachment score\\n    6. Shortest path length (inverse)\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - DataFrame with baseline features for each edge\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    edges = list(G.edges())\\n    features = []\\n    \\n    # Precompute node-based features for efficiency\\n    # Common neighbors\\n    common_neighbors = {}\\n    for u, v in edges:\\n        common_neighbors[(u, v)] = list(nx.common_neighbors(G, u, v))\\n    \\n    # Betweenness centrality (compute once)\\n    edge_betweenness = nx.edge_betweenness_centrality(G)\\n    \\n    for u, v in edges:\\n        # Jaccard coefficient\\n        set_u = set(G.neighbors(u))\\n        set_v = set(G.neighbors(v))\\n        jaccard = len(set_u & set_v) / (len(set_u | set_v) + 1e-10)\\n        \\n        # Adamic-Adar index\\n        adamic_adar = sum(1 / np.log(G.degree(z) + 1) \\n                         for z in common_neighbors.get((u, v), []))\\n        \\n        # Common neighbors count\\n        common_neigh_count = len(common_neighbors.get((u, v), []))\\n        \\n        # Preferential attachment\\n        pref_attach = G.degree(u) * G.degree(v)\\n        \\n        # Shortest path (inverse, handle disconnected)\\n        try:\\n            sp_length = nx.shortest_path_length(G, u, v)\\n            inv_sp = 1.0 / (sp_length + 1e-10)\\n        except nx.NetworkXNoPath:\\n            inv_sp = 0\\n        \\n        feature_dict = {\\n            'edge': (u, v),\\n            'betweenness': edge_betweenness.get((u, v), 0),\\n            'jaccard': jaccard,\\n            'adamic_adar': adamic_adar,\\n            'common_neighbors': common_neigh_count,\\n            'pref_attachment': pref_attach,\\n            'inv_shortest_path': inv_sp\\n        }\\n        features.append(feature_dict)\\n    \\n    return pd.DataFrame(features)\\n\\n\\ndef compute_unsupervised_baselines(G, features_df, y_true, edge_list):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute unsupervised anomaly detection baselines.\\n    \\n    Methods:\\n    1. Local Outlier Factor (LOF)\\n    2. Isolation Forest\\n    3. One-Class SVM\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - Dictionary of method_name -> AUC-ROC score\\n    - Dictionary of method_name -> predicted scores\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Prepare feature matrix\\n    X = features_df[['ollivier_curv', 'forman_curv', 'diff', 'abs_diff']].values\\n    X_scaled = StandardScaler().fit_transform(X)\\n    \\n    results = {}\\n    scores_dict = {}\\n    \\n    # LOF\\n    lof = LocalOutlierFactor(n_neighbors=20, contamination=0.1)\\n    lof_pred = lof.fit_predict(X_scaled)\\n    lof_scores = -lof.negative_outlier_factor_  # Higher = more anomalous\\n    \\n    if len(np.unique(y_true)) > 1:\\n        auc_lof = roc_auc_score(y_true, lof_scores)\\n    else:\\n        auc_lof = 0.5\\n    results['LOF'] = auc_lof\\n    scores_dict['LOF'] = lof_scores\\n    \\n    # Isolation Forest\\n    iso_forest = IsolationForest(contamination=0.1, random_state=42)\\n    iso_pred = iso_forest.fit_predict(X_scaled)\\n    iso_scores = -iso_forest.decision_function(X_scaled)  # Higher = more anomalous\\n    \\n    if len(np.unique(y_true)) > 1:\\n        auc_iso = roc_auc_score(y_true, iso_scores)\\n    else:\\n        auc_iso = 0.5\\n    results['IsolationForest'] = auc_iso\\n    scores_dict['IsolationForest'] = iso_scores\\n    \\n    return results, scores_dict\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 7: Main Classification Pipeline\\n```python\\ndef curvature_discrepancy_classifier(features_df, y_true, edge_list):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Train classifier on curvature discrepancy features.\\n    \\n    Features used:\\n    - diff (Ollivier - Forman)\\n    - abs_diff\\n    - z_score_diff\\n    - ratio\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - Trained classifier\\n    - Cross-validation scores\\n    - Feature importance\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Prepare feature matrix\\n    X = features_df[['diff', 'abs_diff', 'z_score_diff', 'ratio']].values\\n    X_scaled = StandardScaler().fit_transform(X)\\n    \\n    # Train classifier (Random Forest for interpretability)\\n    clf = RandomForestClassifier(n_estimators=100, random_state=42, n_jobs=-1)\\n    \\n    # 5-fold cross-validation\\n    kf = KFold(n_splits=5, shuffle=True, random_state=42)\\n    cv_scores = cross_val_score(clf, X_scaled, y_true, cv=kf, scoring='roc_auc')\\n    \\n    # Train on full data\\n    clf.fit(X_scaled, y_true)\\n    \\n    return clf, cv_scores, clf.feature_importances_\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 8: Statistical Validation\\n```python\\ndef bootstrap_confidence_interval(y_true, y_pred_proba, n_bootstrap=1000, alpha=0.05):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Compute 95% confidence interval for AUC-ROC using bootstrapping.\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - AUC-ROC point estimate\\n    - CI lower bound\\n    - CI upper bound\\n    - Bootstrap distribution (for plotting)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    auc_point = roc_auc_score(y_true, y_pred_proba)\\n    \\n    bootstrap_aucs = []\\n    n_samples = len(y_true)\\n    \\n    for i in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        # Bootstrap sample\\n        indices = np.random.choice(n_samples, size=n_samples, replace=True)\\n        y_true_boot = y_true[indices]\\n        y_pred_boot = y_pred_proba[indices]\\n        \\n        # Only compute if both classes present\\n        if len(np.unique(y_true_boot)) > 1:\\n            auc_boot = roc_auc_score(y_true_boot, y_pred_boot)\\n            bootstrap_aucs.append(auc_boot)\\n    \\n    # Compute confidence interval\\n    lower_idx = int(n_bootstrap * alpha / 2)\\n    upper_idx = int(n_bootstrap * (1 - alpha / 2))\\n    \\n    bootstrap_aucs = np.sort(bootstrap_aucs)\\n    ci_lower = bootstrap_aucs[lower_idx]\\n    ci_upper = bootstrap_aucs[upper_idx]\\n    \\n    return auc_point, ci_lower, ci_upper, bootstrap_aucs\\n\\n\\ndef paired_ttest_baselines(y_true, scores_method1, scores_method2, method1_name, method2_name):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Perform paired t-test to compare two methods.\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - t-statistic\\n    - p-value\\n    - Cohen's d (effect size)\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Compute AUC for each method on bootstrap samples\\n    n_bootstrap = 1000\\n    aucs1 = []\\n    aucs2 = []\\n    n_samples = len(y_true)\\n    \\n    for i in range(n_bootstrap):\\n        indices = np.random.choice(n_samples, size=n_samples, replace=True)\\n        y_true_boot = y_true[indices]\\n        s1_boot = scores_method1[indices]\\n        s2_boot = scores_method2[indices]\\n        \\n        if len(np.unique(y_true_boot)) > 1:\\n            aucs1.append(roc_auc_score(y_true_boot, s1_boot))\\n            aucs2.append(roc_auc_score(y_true_boot, s2_boot))\\n    \\n    # Paired t-test\\n    t_stat, p_value = stats.ttest_rel(aucs1, aucs2)\\n    \\n    # Cohen's d (paired)\\n    diff = np.array(aucs1) - np.array(aucs2)\\n    cohens_d = np.mean(diff) / np.std(diff)\\n    \\n    return t_stat, p_value, cohens_d\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 9: Interpretability Case Studies\\n```python\\ndef generate_interpretability_cases(G, features_df, y_true, edge_list, clf, X_scaled):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Generate interpretability case studies.\\n    \\n    Identify:\\n    - 10 high-discrepancy edges (top predicted anomaly scores)\\n    - 10 low-discrepancy edges (bottom predicted anomaly scores)\\n    \\n    For each edge, show:\\n    - Curvature values (Ollivier, Forman, discrepancy)\\n    - Local neighborhood structure (degrees, triangles)\\n    - Explanation of why anomalous or normal\\n    - Prediction score from classifier\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - Dictionary with case study data\\n    - Path to saved visualization PNG\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Get prediction scores\\n    scores = clf.predict_proba(X_scaled)[:, 1]\\n    \\n    # Add scores to features_df\\n    features_df['anomaly_score'] = scores\\n    features_df['y_true'] = y_true\\n    \\n    # Sort by anomaly score\\n    sorted_df = features_df.sort_values('anomaly_score', ascending=False)\\n    \\n    # Top 10 high-discrepancy (predicted anomalous)\\n    high_discrepancy = sorted_df.head(10)\\n    \\n    # Bottom 10 low-discrepancy (predicted normal)\\n    low_discrepancy = sorted_df.tail(10)\\n    \\n    case_studies = {\\n        'high_discrepancy': [],\\n        'low_discrepancy': []\\n    }\\n    \\n    # Analyze high-discrepancy edges\\n    for idx, row in high_discrepancy.iterrows():\\n        u, v = row['edge']\\n        \\n        # Local neighborhood analysis\\n        neighbors_u = list(G.neighbors(u))\\n        neighbors_v = list(G.neighbors(v))\\n        common_neighbors = list(nx.common_neighbors(G, u, v))\\n        \\n        # Explanation\\n        if row['diff'] > 0:\\n            explanation = f\\\"Ollivier curvature ({row['ollivier_curv']:.4f}) > Forman curvature ({row['forman_curv']:.4f}). \\\"\\n            explanation += \\\"This suggests strong local transport but weak clustering - possible anomalous citation.\\\"\\n        else:\\n            explanation = f\\\"Forman curvature ({row['forman_curv']:.4f}) > Ollivier curvature ({row['ollivier_curv']:.4f}). \\\"\\n            explanation += \\\"Strong clustering but weak transport - possible citation ring.\\\"\\n        \\n        case_studies['high_discrepancy'].append({\\n            'edge': (u, v),\\n            'ollivier_curv': row['ollivier_curv'],\\n            'forman_curv': row['forman_curv'],\\n            'discrepancy': row['diff'],\\n            'anomaly_score': row['anomaly_score'],\\n            'y_true': row['y_true'],\\n            'deg_u': G.degree(u),\\n            'deg_v': G.degree(v),\\n            'common_neighbors': len(common_neighbors),\\n            'explanation': explanation\\n        })\\n    \\n    # Analyze low-discrepancy edges\\n    for idx, row in low_discrepancy.iterrows():\\n        u, v = row['edge']\\n        \\n        neighbors_u = list(G.neighbors(u))\\n        neighbors_v = list(G.neighbors(v))\\n        common_neighbors = list(nx.common_neighbors(G, u, v))\\n        \\n        explanation = f\\\"Curvatures are consistent (diff={row['diff']:.4f}). \\\"\\n        explanation += \\\"Edge appears structurally normal for citation network.\\\"\\n        \\n        case_studies['low_discrepancy'].append({\\n            'edge': (u, v),\\n            'ollivier_curv': row['ollivier_curv'],\\n            'forman_curv': row['forman_curv'],\\n            'discrepancy': row['diff'],\\n            'anomaly_score': row['anomaly_score'],\\n            'y_true': row['y_true'],\\n            'deg_u': G.degree(u),\\n            'deg_v': G.degree(v),\\n            'common_neighbors': len(common_neighbors),\\n            'explanation': explanation\\n        })\\n    \\n    return case_studies\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 10: Visualization Generation\\n```python\\ndef generate_figures(results_dict, output_dir='./figures'):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Generate publication-ready figures.\\n    \\n    Figures:\\n    1. ROC curves for all methods\\n    2. Curvature discrepancy distribution (normal vs anomalous)\\n    3. Case study visualizations\\n    4. Forman)')\\n    plt.ylabel('Density')\\n    plt.title('Distribution of Curvature Discrepancy')\\n    plt.legend()\\n    plt.grid(True, alpha=0.3)\\n    plt.tight_layout()\\n    plt.savefig(f'{output_dir}/discrepancy_distribution.png', dpi=300)\\n    plt.close()\\n    \\n    # Figure 3: Runtime Comparison\\n    plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))\\n    methods = list(results_dict['runtimes'].keys())\\n    runtimes = list(results_dict['runtimes'].values())\\n    \\n    plt.bar(methods, runtimes)\\n    plt.xlabel('Method')\\n    plt.ylabel('Runtime (seconds)')\\n    plt.title('Runtime Comparison')\\n    plt.xticks(rotation=45)\\n    plt.grid(True, alpha=0.3)\\n    plt.tight_layout()\\n    plt.savefig(f'{output_dir}/runtime_comparison.png', dpi=300)\\n    plt.close()\\n```\\n\\n### STEP 11: Main Experiment Loop\\n```python\\ndef run_full_experiment(dataset_path, dataset_name, seeds=[42, 123, 456, 789, 101112, 131415, 161718, 192021, 222324, 252627]):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    Run full experiment with all components.\\n    \\n    Parameters:\\n    - dataset_path: Path to dataset JSON\\n    - dataset_name: 'cora', 'citeseer', or 'pubmed'\\n    - seeds: List of random seeds for robustness\\n    \\n    Returns:\\n    - results_dict: Complete results for method_out.json\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    # Load dataset\\n    with open(dataset_path, 'r') as f:\\n        data = json.load(f)\\n    \\n    # Convert to NetworkX graph\\n    G = nx.Graph()\\n    # ...
